The most common interaction types include:\n\n1. Electrostatic interactions: When a charged guest binds to a host, the local electric field can shift the redox potential of the host or a co-encapsulated redox-active species.\n2. Hydrogen bonding: Formation or disruption of hydrogen bonds between host and guest can modulate electron density and influence redox properties.\n3. π-π stacking: Aromatic hosts and guests can engage in π-π interactions, affecting electron delocalization and redox behavior.\n4.
